Hi Christian,

On 1/6/2015 4:56 AM, Cristian Undurraga wrote:
> Hi Luke,
>
> I´m Cristian Undurraga from Chile, we were talking about our OpenSpim Light Sheet at beginning of the last year.
>
> Some weeks ago (20th Dic) we updated the software but after this we presented problems with the software. The Fiji program didn´t work properly, neither the uManager. We try the update again (22th Dic), Fiji open correctly but now the uManager plugin don`t recognize the devices (Laser, camera and stage control).
>
> We also downloaded again the Fiji package with the last version of OpenSpim but didn`t bring the "stage control" plugin to our Light Sheet .
>
> If you could help us, or other person in OpenSpim who can help us, we would be grateful.
> I send the CoreLog from those days:
I'm afraid I'm no longer active in the development of the OpenSPIM 
platform; I've had to move across the United States for graduate school, 
and I have a very difficult time working remotely while enrolled in 
graduate-level classes. I've forwarded this e-mail onto the OpenSPIM 
mailing list (openspim at openspim.org), where it should reach people much 
more familiar with the current state of the project than I am. (I 
suggest CCing that list in the future as well; they'll be able to 
provide more up-to-date help more quickly than I can.)

That said, here's the problems I see, based on your most recent core log:
- The camera (OrcaFlash) is failing to initialize (line 227): "Error 
code 40 (28 hex)." (Sadly I've no idea what precisely that error code 
means. It may be the memory bug rearing its head again, so perhaps 
limiting Fiji's memory will solve this.)
- The laser (Cobolt) is having an error when the program asks whether or 
not it's turned on (line 339). This leads to a number of errors, since 
the laser is in an invalid state -- for instance on lines 415 and, when 
OpenSPIM is loading, 819. (This second error I've seen before, but I 
don't recall the fix -- I believed it was a bug in the Cobolt device 
adapter at the time.)

As usual, please make sure your Fiji and OpenSPIM are completely 
up-to-date by running the Fiji updater. (I usually run it, restart Fiji, 
then repeat until the updater says Fiji is up-to-date.)

My best suggestion for an immediate fix would be to re-make your 
configuration file according to the process on our wiki. (It may help to 
select 'none' as the configuration file when Micro-Manager is opening.) 
It's possible that device adapter names or their property names have 
changed, so doing this might create a working configuration file.

However, as I understand it, some significant development has been 
happening on OpenSPIM recently to improve its relationship to 
Micro-Manager (which will probably lead to 64-bit OpenSPIM, among other 
benefits!). Not all the changes may be in the updater; it's also 
possible the installation process has changed entirely. Hopefully the 
mailing list can offer some advice on this point.

Hope this helps,
Luke Stuyvenberg
